<div id="review_1750394539" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1750394539" />
    <a title="Martin Haynes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28889577-martin-haynes"><img alt="Martin Haynes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544636794p2/28889577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1750394539?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Martin Haynes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Martin Haynes" href="/user/show/28889577-martin-haynes">Martin Haynes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1750394539" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer705856695519752482">Two main problems with this one. The political background to the early part of the book had been outstripped by developments of the last decade or so and the book is reminiscent of a previous Stephen Baxter book that I read. Having said that, the central idea behind the book is quite interesting. How would we cope in a world when you could be watched by anyone at any time and how would we cope when your past could be viewed by anyone? Scary propositions!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2045584969" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2045584969?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chak" href="/user/show/962423-chak">Chak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/962423-chak?shelf=sci-fi-and-fantasy">sci-fi-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/962423-chak?shelf=ymca-share-a-book">ymca-share-a-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/962423-chak?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/962423-chak?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2045584969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10319483914678073251">Yet again, Clarke gave me what I have come to expect from him -- a huge concept regarding the human condition (privacy, ownership, control, evolution), a glimpse into a near-incomprehensible time-span <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[(but this time, it was backwards instead of forward!) <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and a gripping, thrilling story. <br/><br/>The concepts in this book will continue to stay with me for a very long time, if not forever. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I have always tried to consider my impact on the future. However, after</span></span>
  <span id="freeText10319483914678073251" style="display:none">Yet again, Clarke gave me what I have come to expect from him -- a huge concept regarding the human condition (privacy, ownership, control, evolution), a glimpse into a near-incomprehensible time-span <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(but this time, it was backwards instead of forward!) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and a gripping, thrilling story. <br /><br />The concepts in this book will continue to stay with me for a very long time, if not forever. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I have always tried to consider my impact on the future. However, after reading this, I am now considering how the future might <b><i>literally <u>see</u></i></b> me, and that is a sobering and humbling thought! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I highly recommend this book as a "good read" -- not only for the story, and for the philosophy, but also to marvel at how much Clarke and Baxter got right about what happened over the next few years of our (real) history (note: this book was first published in 2000).<br /><br />Some notable passages:<br /><br /><b>p. 115 (Kate and Bobby are talking)</b><br />"...Of course it's disturbing. A technology of such power--"<br /><br />"But you were there when we came to our agreement with the FBI. An agreement that put the WormCam in the hands of the people."<br /><br />"Oh, Bobby... <i>The people</i> don't even know the damn thing exists, let alone that government agencies are using it against them. Look at all the tax defaulters that suddenly got caught, the parents cheating on child support, the Brady Law checks on gun buyers, the serial sex offenders."<br /><br />"But that's all for the good. Isn't it? What are you saying -- that you don't trust the government? This isn't the twentieth century."<br /><br />She grunted. "Remember what Jefferson said: 'Every government degenerates when trusted to the rulers of the people alone. The people themselves therefore are its only safe depositories.' ...."<br /><br /><b>p. 165 (Hiram and David are talking)</b><br />"...By showing us the <i>destination</i>, without requiring of us the enervating <i>journey</i>, the WormCam will turn us into a planet of couch potatoes. ... Now we have the WormCam, and we don't need to deduce anymore, to strive, to <i>think</i>."<br /><br />"Isn't that a good thing?"<br /><br />"No!" David snapped. "It is like a child turning to the answers at the back of an exercise book. The point, you see, is not the answers themselves, but the mental development we enjoy through striving for those answers. ... Science will become taxonomy."<br /><br /><b>p. 174</b><br />... there was no accepted definition of privacy rights, even within America. Privacy was not mentioned in the Constitution. The Fourth Amendment to the Bill of Rights spoke of a right against intrusion by the state -- but it left a great deal of room for maneuver by those in authority who wished to investigate citizens, and besides offered citizens virtually no protection against other bodies, such as corporations or the press or even other citizens. <br /><br /><b>p. 215</b><br />We must wonder where this will lead us. Just as the human memory is not a passive recorder but a tool in the construction of the self, so history has never been a simple record of the past, but a means of shaping peoples.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2439498891" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2439498891" />
    <a title="Malcolm Little" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33017722-malcolm-little"><img alt="Malcolm Little" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451086212p2/33017722.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2439498891?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Malcolm Little" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Malcolm Little" href="/user/show/33017722-malcolm-little">Malcolm Little</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006483748" href="/book/show/64015.The_Light_Of_Other_Days">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2439498891" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6095405082835121275">I admit, I’m biased towards both authors of Light of Other Days. Clarke needs no explanation, and Baxter is one of those ideas men that rise above the crowd, as he can deliver the goods in both a sweeping scope and an intimate flair. Coming in, I was expecting to be blown away by this collaboration between two of space opera’s most seminal artists. <br/><br/>It didn’t happen.<br/><br/>Now, the wormcam concept – essentially time-travel-like viewing through quantum tunneling – is a very interesting scientific thought</span>
  <span id="freeText6095405082835121275" style="display:none">I admit, I’m biased towards both authors of Light of Other Days. Clarke needs no explanation, and Baxter is one of those ideas men that rise above the crowd, as he can deliver the goods in both a sweeping scope and an intimate flair. Coming in, I was expecting to be blown away by this collaboration between two of space opera’s most seminal artists. <br /><br />It didn’t happen.<br /><br />Now, the wormcam concept – essentially time-travel-like viewing through quantum tunneling – is a very interesting scientific thought experiment of the possible uses of wormholes. The social manifestations of these developments are described in aplomb, as are the immense revisions of history that undoubtedly would occur. The basic hard sci-fi foundations are, of course, sound and fascinating, supported by plausible snippets of technical explanations and executions. The early chapters, where the wormcam's potential is gradually being realized, are satisfying and hint at greater things to come. Sometimes those greater things materialize with the aforementioned flair both authors possess. <br /><br />Nevertheless, as a work of fiction, which necessarily involves depth of character, themes on the human condition, and a progression of plot affecting those characters and the settings they find themselves in, the book utterly fails. The gaggle of protagonists &amp; antagonists are hardly more than clichés, with the depth of a Tucson puddle. The occasional excessive chapters, devoted to the political intrigue and human-interest stories revolving around wormcam development, utterly failed to impress. I simply couldn't get worked up at all about what happened to the stereotypical fatcat capitalist, his religiously monotone son, the wormcam addicts, or even the woman investigator with a heart of gold. There was no empathy, sympathy, or intrigue to be had among the collection of biodegradable mats representing the cast of Light. <br /><br />So what can be salvaged from Light of Other Days. As one might expect, the exposition on the possibilities of future technologies. Clarke is a lighthouse when it comes to writing about such phenomenon; he’s practically Nostradamus in his prognostications. What is discussed in this book, published in the year 2000, might strike some as prescient, especially in these halcyon social media days – days where polls of those who’ve formative years lack any old semblance of privacy. <br /><br />Habituation to something like the wormcam is startlingly possible. Clarke and Baxter had this feeling, and hash out the consequences of such an approach. That is where the strength in Light lies, and when the utilization of the wormcam gets rolling, it becomes an avalanche that sparks the imagination. Light is an ideas book, powered by the science aspect of science fiction, dumping the fiction on the side of the road. A non-fiction novelette might have been a better fit for what the duo wanted to talk about. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6095405082835121275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Qg8HKAICDZ3i338NNifRYBmmSOUHwZv2dq623nK1jnemn60hO2Sz9gsbIcoXQodscsQxGtuAhyZbab/lEFwWdg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZrNazDtmAAEDWoxqeXy9kJG33fqT+EWBxSwYu2BFU3uCI/DFAgC+auqe0q1YGeuc+tWkBU+5WVHo6xGAAqzLeg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7779.Arthur_C_Clarke">About Arthur C. Clarke</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7779.Arthur_C_Clarke"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1357191481p3/7779.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7779.Arthur_C_Clarke">Arthur C. Clarke
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
8,240
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer149823586567702534">Arthur Charles Clarke was one of the most important and influential figures in 20th century science fiction. He spent the first half of his life in England, where he served in World War Two as a radar operator, before emigrating to Ceylon in 1956. He is best known for the novel and movie <i>2001: A Space Odyssey</i>, which he co-created with the assistance of Stanley Kubrick.<br/><br/>Clarke was a graduate of King</span>
  <span id="freeText149823586567702534" style="display:none">Arthur Charles Clarke was one of the most important and influential figures in 20th century science fiction. He spent the first half of his life in England, where he served in World War Two as a radar operator, before emigrating to Ceylon in 1956. He is best known for the novel and movie <i>2001: A Space Odyssey</i>, which he co-created with the assistance of Stanley Kubrick.<br /><br />Clarke was a graduate of King's College, London where he obtained First Class Honours in Physics and Mathematics. He is past Chairman of the British Interplanetary Society, a member of the Academy of Astronautics, the Royal Astronomical Society, and many other scientific organizations.<br /><br />Author of over fifty books, his numerous awards include the 1961 Kalinga Prize, the AAAS-Westinghouse science writing prize, the Bradford Washburn Award, and the John W. Campbell Award for his novel <i>Rendezvous With Rama</i>. Clarke also won the Nebula Award of the Science Fiction Writers of America in 1972, 1974 and 1979, the Hugo Award of the World Science Fiction Convention in 1974 and 1980, and in 1986 became Grand Master of the Science Fiction Writers of America. He was awarded the CBE in 1989.</span>
  <a data-text-id="149823586567702534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
